Transcript:  You got two different Carolinas, two Virginias, and two Dakotas, so, what's the reason for all these stats dividing? Well, for two of these cases, the answer is pretty straightforward.

For example, North Carolina and South Carolina were both once part of the British territory of Carolina, and mutually agreed to split mainly because of differing economic focuses.
Similarly, both North and South Dakota were once part of the large Dakota Territory, and split up for the simple reason that splitting into two states would allow for more representation in congress than if they had stayed together.

However, when it comes to why Virginia and West Virginia are two different states, the answer becomes a little more interesting. You see, instead of a territory simply being carved up, this split actually resulted from West Virginia forcefully seceding from Virginia.

And to understand why, we need to go back to the early 1860s, when, nearing the beginning of the civil war, Virginia broke away from the Northern US to join the Confederate States of the South. However, many people in the northwest of Virginia were still loyal to the Union, so they severed ties with the rest of the state, and were admitted to the union as a brand new one. Although, because of their shared history, they decided to keep the same name.
